   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Equation of state
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=State_equation&amp;redirect=no" title="State equation">
       State equation
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       For the use of this in cosmology, see
       <a href="/wiki/Equation_of_state_(cosmology)" title="Equation of state (cosmology)">
        Equation of state (cosmology)
       </a>
       . For the use of this concept in optimal control theory, see
       <a href="/wiki/Optimal_control#General_method" title="Optimal control">
        Optimal control § General method
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">
        physics
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamics" title="Thermodynamics">
        thermodynamics
       </a>
       , an
       <b>
        equation of state
       </b>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_equations" title="Thermodynamic equations">
        thermodynamic equation
       </a>
       relating
       <a href="/wiki/State_variable" title="State variable">
        state variables
       </a>
       which describe the state of matter under a given set of physical conditions, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">
        pressure
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Volume_(thermodynamics)" title="Volume (thermodynamics)">
        volume
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">
        temperature
       </a>
       (
       <b>
        PVT
       </b>
       ), or
       <a href="/wiki/Internal_energy" title="Internal energy">
        internal energy
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perrot_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Perrot-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Equations of state are useful in describing the properties of
       <a href="/wiki/Fluid" title="Fluid">
        fluids
       </a>
       , mixtures of fluids,
       <a href="/wiki/Solid" title="Solid">
        solids
       </a>
       , and the interior of
       <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">
        stars
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks plainlist" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%">
       <tr>
        <th style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.2em;font-size:145%;line-height:1.2em;padding-bottom:0.3em;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">

          Thermodynamics
         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;display:block;margin:0.3em 0 0.4em;">

         </a>
         <div style="padding-top:0.2em;line-height:1.2em">

               <img alt="A(T,V)=U-TS" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5e93692f031ba6484d82731c54db83a69daed3f0" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.867ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
              </span>
             </li>
             <li style="font-size:110%;line-height:1.6em;padding-bottom:0.5em;">

               Gibbs free energy
              </a>
              <br/>
              <span class="mwe-math-element">
               <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
                <math alttext="{\displaystyle G(T,p)=H-TS}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

                   <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

                     (

                     )

           <a href="#Jones–Wilkins–Lee_equation_of_state_for_explosives_(JWL_equation)">
            <span class="tocnumber">
             9.4
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Jones–Wilkins–Lee equation of state for explosives (JWL equation)
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33">
         <a href="#Equations_of_state_for_solids_and_liquids">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           10
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Equations of state for solids and liquids
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34">
         <a href="#See_also">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           11
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           See also
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35">
         <a href="#References">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           12
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           References
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">
        Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The most prominent use of an equation of state is to correlate densities of gases and liquids to temperatures and pressures. One of the simplest equations of state for this purpose is the
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas_law" title="Ideal gas law">
        ideal gas law
       </a>
       , which is roughly accurate for weakly polar gases at low pressures and moderate temperatures. However, this equation becomes increasingly inaccurate at higher pressures and lower temperatures, and fails to predict condensation from a gas to a liquid. Therefore, a number of more accurate equations of state have been developed for gases and liquids. At present, there is no single equation of state that accurately predicts the properties of all substances under all conditions.
      </p>
      <p>
       <span id="lasers2016-01-29">
       </span>
       Measurements of equation-of-state parameters, especially at high pressures, can be made using lasers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition, there are also equations of state describing solids, including the transition of solids from one crystalline state to another. There are equations that model the interior of stars, including
       <a href="/wiki/Neutron_star" title="Neutron star">
        neutron stars
       </a>
       , dense matter (
       <a href="/wiki/Quark%E2%80%93gluon_plasma" title="Quark–gluon plasma">
        quark–gluon plasmas
       </a>
       ) and radiation fields. A related concept is the
       <a href="/wiki/Perfect_fluid" title="Perfect fluid">
        perfect fluid
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Equation_of_state_(cosmology)" title="Equation of state (cosmology)">
        equation of state used in cosmology
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In practical context, the equations of state are instrumental for PVT calculation in process engineering problems and especially in petroleum gas/liquid equilibrium calculations. A successful PVT model based on a fitting equation of state can be helpful to determine the state of the flow regime, the parameters for handling the
       <a href="/wiki/Reservoir_fluids" title="Reservoir fluids">
        reservoir fluids
       </a>
       , piping and sizing.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical">
        Historical
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Historical">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span id="Boyle.27s_law_.281662.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Boyle's_law_(1662)">
        Boyle's law (1662)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Boyle's law (1662)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Boyle's Law was perhaps the first expression of an equation of state.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In 1662, the Irish physicist and chemist
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Boyle" title="Robert Boyle">
        Robert Boyle
       </a>
       performed a series of experiments employing a J-shaped glass tube, which was sealed on one end.
       <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">
        Mercury
       </a>
       was added to the tube, trapping a fixed quantity of air in the short, sealed end of the tube. Then the volume of gas was measured as additional mercury was added to the tube. The pressure of the gas could be determined by the difference between the mercury level in the short end of the tube and that in the long, open end. Through these experiments, Boyle noted that the gas volume varied inversely with the pressure. In mathematical form, this can be stated as:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle pV=\mathrm {constant} .\,\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mi>
               V
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                c
               </mi>
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                o
               </mi>
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                n
               </mi>
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                s
               </mi>
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                t
               </mi>
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                a
               </mi>
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                n
               </mi>
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                t
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle pV=\mathrm {constant} .\,\!}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="pV={\mathrm  {constant}}.\,\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/905f8727239dee1d3700ee4caac1e0b34b66e619" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:15.846ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The above relationship has also been attributed to
       <a href="/wiki/Edme_Mariotte" title="Edme Mariotte">
        Edme Mariotte
       </a>
       and is sometimes referred to as Mariotte's law. However, Mariotte's work was not published until 1676.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Charles.27s_law_or_Law_of_Charles_and_Gay-Lussac_.281787.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Charles's_law_or_Law_of_Charles_and_Gay-Lussac_(1787)">
        Charles's law or Law of Charles and Gay-Lussac (1787)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Charles's law or Law of Charles and Gay-Lussac (1787)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1787 the French physicist
       <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Charles" title="Jacques Charles">
        Jacques Charles
       </a>
       found that oxygen, nitrogen, hydrogen, carbon dioxide, and air expand to roughly the same extent over the same 80-kelvin interval. Later, in 1802,
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Louis_Gay-Lussac" title="Joseph Louis Gay-Lussac">
        Joseph Louis Gay-Lussac
       </a>
       published results of similar experiments, indicating a linear relationship between volume and temperature:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {V_{1}}{T_{1}}}={\frac {V_{2}}{T_{2}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  V
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   1
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  T
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   1
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  V
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  T
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\frac {V_{1}}{T_{1}}}={\frac {V_{2}}{T_{2}}}.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\frac  {V_{1}}{T_{1}}}={\frac  {V_{2}}{T_{2}}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86e0ec7f280021fca44ede90829fd4ce78f38436" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:10.241ex; height:5.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h3>
       <span id="Dalton.27s_law_of_partial_pressures_.281801.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dalton's_law_of_partial_pressures_(1801)">
        Dalton's law of partial pressures (1801)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Dalton's law of partial pressures (1801)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dalton%27s_Law" title="Dalton's Law">
        Dalton's Law
       </a>
       of partial pressure states that the pressure of a mixture of gases is equal to the sum of the pressures of all of the constituent gases alone.
      </p>
      <p>
       Mathematically, this can be represented for
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       species as:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <span class="mwe-math-element">
           <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
            <math alttext="{\displaystyle p_{\text{total}}=p_{1}+p_{2}+\cdots +p_{n}=p_{\text{total}}=\sum _{i=1}^{n}p_{i}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
             <semantics>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>
                   total
                  </mtext>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mo>
                 =
                </mo>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   1
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <mo>
                 ⋯
                 <!-- ⋯ -->
                </mo>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   n
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mo>
                 =
                </mo>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>
                   total
                  </mtext>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mo>
                 =
                </mo>
                <munderover>
                 <mo>
                  ∑
                  <!-- ∑ -->
                 </mo>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   i
                  </mi>
                  <mo>
                   =
                  </mo>
                  <mn>
                   1
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   n
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </munderover>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   i
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mo>
                 .
                </mo>
               </mstyle>
              </mrow>
              <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
               {\displaystyle p_{\text{total}}=p_{1}+p_{2}+\cdots +p_{n}=p_{\text{total}}=\sum _{i=1}^{n}p_{i}.}
              </annotation>
             </semantics>
            </math>
           </span>
           <img alt="p_{{\text{total}}}=p_{1}+p_{2}+\cdots +p_{n}=p_{{\text{total}}}=\sum _{{i=1}}^{n}p_{i}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9a2592bef017d129649d3dbceea9f3a97cb91e8f" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:43.387ex; height:6.843ex;"/>
          </span>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h3>
       <span id="The_ideal_gas_law_.281834.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_ideal_gas_law_(1834)">
        The ideal gas law (1834)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The ideal gas law (1834)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1834
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Clapeyron" title="Émile Clapeyron">
        Émile Clapeyron
       </a>
       combined Boyle's Law and Charles' law into the first statement of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas_law" title="Ideal gas law">
         ideal gas law
        </a>
       </i>
       . Initially, the law was formulated as
       <i>
        pV
        <sub>
         m
        </sub>
       </i>
       =
       <i>
        R
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        T
        <sub>
         C
        </sub>
       </i>
       + 267) (with temperature expressed in degrees Celsius), where
       <i>
        R
       </i>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Gas_constant" title="Gas constant">
        gas constant
       </a>
       . However, later work revealed that the number should actually be closer to 273.2, and then the Celsius scale was defined with 0 °C = 273.15 K, giving:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \ pV_{m}=R(T_{C}+273.15^{\circ }C).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mtext>
              </mtext>
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               R
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                T
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 C
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <msup>
               <mn>
                273.15
               </mn>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mo>
                 ∘
                 <!-- ∘ -->
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \ pV_{m}=R(T_{C}+273.15^{\circ }C).}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle \ pV_{m}=R(T_{C}+273.15^{\circ }C).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3991d04b0dc3dbb54839c9f5b509969cfa415b3c" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:27.058ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h3>
       <span id="Van_der_Waals_equation_of_state_.281873.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Van_der_Waals_equation_of_state_(1873)">
        Van der Waals equation of state (1873)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Van der Waals equation of state (1873)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1873,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._D._van_der_Waals" title="J. D. van der Waals">
        J. D. van der Waals
       </a>
       introduced the first
       <a href="/wiki/Van_der_Waals_equation" title="Van der Waals equation">
        equation of state
       </a>
       derived by the assumption of a finite volume occupied by the constituent molecules.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_der_Waals_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-van_der_Waals-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His new formula revolutionized the study of equations of state, and was most famously continued via the
       <a href="/wiki/Redlich%E2%80%93Kwong_equation_of_state" title="Redlich–Kwong equation of state">
        Redlich–Kwong equation of state
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="#Soave_modification_of_Redlich-Kwong">
        Soave modification of Redlich-Kwong
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_equations_of_state">
        Major equations of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Major equations of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       For a given amount of substance contained in a system, the temperature, volume, and pressure are not independent quantities; they are connected by a relationship of the general form:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\ f(p,V,T)=0}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mtext>
               </mtext>
               <mi>
                f
               </mi>
               <mo stretchy="false">
                (
               </mo>
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
               <mo>
                ,
               </mo>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mo>
                ,
               </mo>
               <mi>
                T
               </mi>
               <mo stretchy="false">
                )
               </mo>
               <mo>
                =
               </mo>
               <mn>
                0
               </mn>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\ f(p,V,T)=0}.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\ f(p,V,T)=0}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ede2e23d1e0ed84e66a2fa9dfdb86e7ad07dcbaa" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.237ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       In the following equations the variables are defined as follows. Any consistent set of units may be used, although
       <a href="/wiki/International_System_of_Units" title="International System of Units">
        SI
       </a>
       units are preferred.
       <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_temperature" title="Thermodynamic temperature">
        Absolute temperature
       </a>
       refers to use of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kelvin" title="Kelvin">
        Kelvin
       </a>
       (K) or
       <a href="/wiki/Rankine_scale" title="Rankine scale">
        Rankine
       </a>
       (°R) temperature scales, with zero being absolute zero.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \ p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mtext>
              </mtext>

              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \ p}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\ p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f385a789c147f05d215d99fecd7ff19e8fd40b05" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.75ex; height:2.009ex;"/>
        </span>
        = pressure (absolute)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \ V}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mtext>
              </mtext>

              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>

           </semantics>
          </math>

        </span>
        = volume
       </dd>
       <dd>

        </span>
        = number of moles of a substance
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">

        </span>
        =
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

            </annotation>

        </span>
        =
        <b>

        </span>

        <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_temperature" title="Thermodynamic temperature">

        (8.3144621 J/(mol·K))

        </span>
        = pressure at the critical point

        </span>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_ideal_gas_law">
        Classical ideal gas law
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Classical ideal gas law">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The classical
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas_law" title="Ideal gas law">
        ideal gas law
       </a>
       may be written:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\ pV=nRT}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mtext>
               </mtext>
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mo>
                =
               </mo>
               <mi>
                n
               </mi>
               <mi>
                R
               </mi>
               <mi>
                T
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\ pV=nRT}.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\ pV=nRT}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1d265b7474ea773feacba0e1b4a7cfba37881403" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.078ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       In the form shown above, the equation of state is thus
      </p>
      <p>
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle f(p,V,T)=pV-nRT=0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              f
             </mi>
             <mo stretchy="false">
              (
             </mo>
             <mi>
              p
             </mi>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <mi>
              V
             </mi>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <mi>
              T
             </mi>
             <mo stretchy="false">
              )
             </mo>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <mi>
              p
             </mi>
             <mi>
              V
             </mi>
             <mo>
              −
              <!-- − -->
             </mo>
             <mi>
              n
             </mi>
             <mi>
              R
             </mi>
             <mi>
              T
             </mi>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <mn>
              0
             </mn>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle f(p,V,T)=pV-nRT=0}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="f(p,V,T)=pV-nRT=0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e036f357c47130b55fc8d7ceae39ebec2114ff51" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:27.7ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       If the
       <a href="/wiki/Perfect_gas" title="Perfect gas">
        calorically perfect
       </a>
       gas approximation is used, then the ideal gas law may also be expressed as follows
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\ p=\rho (\gamma -1)e}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mtext>
               </mtext>
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
               <mo>
                =
               </mo>
               <mi>
                ρ
                <!-- ρ -->
               </mi>
               <mo stretchy="false">
                (
               </mo>
               <mi>
                γ
                <!-- γ -->
               </mi>
               <mo>
                −
                <!-- − -->
               </mo>
               <mn>
                1
               </mn>
               <mo stretchy="false">
                )
               </mo>
               <mi>
                e
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\ p=\rho (\gamma -1)e}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\ p=\rho (\gamma -1)e}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ff900c7745371008152ad511f72f5b2fbd793e51" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:14.208ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \rho }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              ρ
              <!-- ρ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \rho }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\rho " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f7d439671d1289b6a816e6af7a304be40608d64" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:1.202ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the density,
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \gamma =C_{p}/C_{v}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              γ
              <!-- γ -->
             </mi>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mo>
               /
              </mo>
             </mrow>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                v
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \gamma =C_{p}/C_{v}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\gamma =C_{p}/C_{v}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54a4d62c8c5abcb9be36a572f789822f27fafc8c" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:10.936ex; height:3.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the adiabatic index (
       <a href="/wiki/Heat_capacity_ratio" title="Heat capacity ratio">
        ratio of specific heats
       </a>
       ),
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle e=C_{v}T}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              e
             </mi>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                v
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mi>
              T
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle e=C_{v}T}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="e=C_{v}T" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/545752b50cd5343b602a55f4791800703ef96511" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.51ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the internal energy per unit mass (the "specific internal energy"),
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle C_{v}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                v
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle C_{v}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="C_{v}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4e351d30ded09e7d285c21e836f116e14ad5ae28" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.691ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the specific heat at constant volume, and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle C_{p}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle C_{p}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="C_{p}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6bc37470431fbf62081b69ba870ad3f855178361" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.721ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the specific heat at constant pressure.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cubic_equations_of_state">
        Cubic equations of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cubic equations of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Cubic equations of state are called such because they can be rewritten as a
       <a href="/wiki/Cubic_function" title="Cubic function">
        cubic function
       </a>
       of V
       <sub>
        m
       </sub>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Van_der_Waals_equation_of_state">
        Van der Waals equation of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Van der Waals equation of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Van_der_Waals_equation" title="Van der Waals equation">
        Van der Waals equation
       </a>
       of state may be written:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

                </mo>
               </mrow>
               <mrow>
                <mo>
                 (
                </mo>
                <mrow>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   V
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>

                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                 <mo>
                  −
                  <!-- − -->
                 </mo>
                 <mi>
                  b
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mo>

                </mo>
               </mrow>
               <mo>

               </mo>
               <mi>
                R
               </mi>
               <mi>
                T
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>

        </span>

       <span class="mwe-math-element">

        </span>

      <p>
       Also written as
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle a={\frac {27(R\,T_{c})^{2}}{64p_{c}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               a
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mn>
                  27
                 </mn>
                 <mo stretchy="false">
                  (
                 </mo>

                  <mo stretchy="false">

                  </mo>

        </span>

         <img alt="b = \frac{R\,T_c}{8p_c}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4616088a19a4d84c5044747541c140bb0a75313f" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:10.032ex; height:5.676ex;"/>
        </span>

      </dl>
      <p>
       Proposed in 1873, the van der Waals equation of state was one of the first to perform markedly better than the ideal gas law. In this landmark equation
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              a
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle a}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/>
       </span>
       is called the attraction parameter and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              b
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle b}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="b" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f11423fbb2e967f986e36804a8ae4271734917c3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.998ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       the repulsion parameter or the effective molecular volume. While the equation is definitely superior to the ideal gas law and does predict the formation of a liquid phase, the agreement with experimental data is limited for conditions where the liquid forms. While the van der Waals equation is commonly referenced in text-books and papers for historical reasons, it is now obsolete. Other modern equations of only slightly greater complexity are much more accurate.
      </p>
      <p>
       The van der Waals equation may be considered as the ideal gas law, "improved" due to two independent reasons:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Molecules are thought as particles with volume, not material points. Thus
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle V_{m}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle V_{m}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="V_{m}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/40836783b20c374654ab03ddd6b01586ad9b4fb8" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.03ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
        cannot be too little, less than some constant. So we get (
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle V_{m}-b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mi>
               b
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle V_{m}-b}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="V_m - b" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/07b93d1ef8cbc8d7feb9f02a8783bad3be0df03d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.868ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
        ) instead of
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle V_{m}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle V_{m}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="V_{m}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/40836783b20c374654ab03ddd6b01586ad9b4fb8" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.03ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        While ideal gas molecules do not interact, we consider molecules attracting others within a distance of several molecules' radii. It makes no effect inside the material, but surface molecules are attracted into the material from the surface. We see this as diminishing of pressure on the outer shell (which is used in the ideal gas law), so we write (
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle p+}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle p+}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="p +" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/000e23a2df985729599ebeaa4ccf12d7dd16566f" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:3.067ex; height:2.343ex;"/>
        </span>
        something) instead of
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle p}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;"/>
        </span>
        . To evaluate this ‘something’, let's examine an additional force acting on an element of gas surface. While the force acting on each surface molecule is ~
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \rho }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \rho }
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\rho " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f7d439671d1289b6a816e6af7a304be40608d64" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:1.202ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
        </span>
        , the force acting on the whole element is ~
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \rho ^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msup>
               <mi>
                ρ
                <!-- ρ -->
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \rho ^{2}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>

        </span>
        ~
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {1}{V_{m}^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

        </span>
        .
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       With the reduced state variables, i.e. V
       <sub>
        r
       </sub>
       =V
       <sub>
        m
       </sub>
       /V
       <sub>
        c
       </sub>

       <sub>
        r
       </sub>
       =P/P
       <sub>
        c
       </sub>

       <sub>

       </sub>

       <sub>

       </sub>

      <p>
       The benefit of this form is that for given T
       <sub>
        r
       </sub>
       and P
       <sub>
        r
       </sub>
       , the reduced volume of the liquid and gas can be calculated directly using

        Cardano's method
       </a>

      <p>
       For P
       <sub>
        r
       </sub>
       &lt;1 and T
       <sub>
        r
       </sub>
       &lt;1, the system is in a state of vapor–liquid equilibrium. The reduced cubic equation of state yields in that case 3 solutions. The largest and the lowest solution are the gas and liquid reduced volume.
      </p>

                  </mi>

            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="b = \frac{0.08664\,R\,T_c}{p_c}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9e78bd0e0918e12079e6edc2ed13ceb614a3ba8d" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:17.394ex; height:5.676ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Introduced in 1949, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Redlich-Kwong_equation_of_state" title="Redlich-Kwong equation of state">
        Redlich-Kwong equation of state
       </a>
       was a considerable improvement over other equations of the time. It is still of interest primarily due to its relatively simple form. While superior to the van der Waals equation of state, it performs poorly with respect to the liquid phase and thus cannot be used for accurately calculating
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vapor%E2%80%93liquid_equilibria" title="Vapor–liquid equilibria">
        vapor–liquid equilibria
       </a>
       . However, it can be used in conjunction with separate liquid-phase correlations for this purpose.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Redlich-Kwong equation is adequate for calculation of gas phase properties when the ratio of the pressure to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critical_properties" title="Critical properties">
        critical pressure
       </a>
       (reduced pressure) is less than about one-half of the ratio of the temperature to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critical_properties" title="Critical properties">
        critical temperature
       </a>
       (reduced temperature):
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>

      <p>
       Where ω is the
       <a href="/wiki/Acentric_factor" title="Acentric factor">
        acentric factor
       </a>
       for the species.
      </p>
      <p>
       This formulation for
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \alpha }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

       </span>
       is due to Graboski and Daubert. The original formulation from Soave is:

      <p>
       We can also write it in the polynomial form, with:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">

                 </mi>

        </span>

           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               B
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  b
                 </mi>
                 <mspace width="thinmathspace">
                 </mspace>
                 <mi>
                  P
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  R
                 </mi>
                 <mspace width="thinmathspace">
                 </mspace>
                 <mi>
                  T
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle B={\frac {b\,P}{R\,T}}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="B = \frac{b\,P}{R\,T}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8d29cf8a0bacd5455703590b335e65defbc6c1c" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:9.486ex; height:5.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       then we have:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle 0=Z^{3}-Z^{2}+Z\left(A-B-B^{2}\right)-AB\;}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mn>
               0
              </mn>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                Z
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 3
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                Z
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mi>

              </mi>

               </mo>

                </mo>

                </mi>

                </mo>

                 <mi>

                 </mi>

                 </mrow>

               </mrow>

         </span>
         <img alt="0 = Z^3-Z^2+Z\left(A-B-B^2\right)-AB \;" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7270ff697ebc326459cb7e0b42ce03411ffab7e0" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:38.663ex; height:3.343ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle R}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              R
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle R}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="R" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4b0bfb3769bf24d80e15374dc37b0441e2616e33" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_gas_constant" title="Universal gas constant">
        universal gas constant
       </a>
       and Z=PV/(RT) is the
       <a href="/wiki/Compressibility_factor" title="Compressibility factor">
        compressibility factor
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1972 G. Soave
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       replaced the 1/
       <span class="nowrap">
        √
        <span style="border-top:1px solid; padding:0 0.1em;">
         <i>
          T
         </i>
        </span>
       </span>
       term of the Redlich-Kwong equation with a function α(T,ω) involving the temperature and the
       <a href="/wiki/Acentric_factor" title="Acentric factor">
        acentric factor
       </a>
       (the resulting equation is also known as the Soave-Redlich-Kwong equation of state; SRK EOS). The α function was devised to fit the vapor pressure data of hydrocarbons and the equation does fairly well for these materials.
      </p>
      <p>
       Note especially that this replacement changes the definition of
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       slightly, as the
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle T_{c}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                c
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle T_{c}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="T_{c}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/66261e3cbed8035b2bf7a9ccb878c786cf7556c6" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.302ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
       </span>
       is now to the second power.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Volume_translation_of_Peneloux_et_alios">
        Volume translation of Peneloux et alios
       </span>

        </span>

          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle a=a_{c}\,\alpha }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fd24828cac7975fd3d09f50b73e8f2630c314a49" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.377ex; height:2.009ex;"/>
        </span>

       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \alpha }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              α
              <!-- α -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \alpha }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\alpha " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b79333175c8b3f0840bfb4ec41b8072c83ea88d3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.488ex; height:1.676ex;"/>
       </span>
       and other parts of the SRK EOS is defined in the SRK EOS section.
      </p>
      <p>
       A downside of the SRK EOS, and other cubic EOS, is that the liquid molar volume is significantly less accurate than the gas molar volume. Peneloux et alios (1982)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peneloux1982_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Peneloux1982-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       proposed a simple correction for this by introducing a volume translation
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle V_{mSRK}=V_{m}+c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 S
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 R
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 K
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mi>
               c
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle V_{mSRK}=V_{m}+c}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle V_{mSRK}=V_{m}+c}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/14efc37b5ea314415f42f40b0bfacc2719e5652f" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:16.775ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              c
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle c}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/>
       </span>
       is an additional fluid component parameter that translate the molar volume slightly. On the liquid branch of the EOS, a small change in molar volume corresponds to a large change in pressure. On the gas branch of the EOS, a small change in molar volume corresponds to a much smaller change in pressure than for the liquid branch. Thus, the perturbation of the molar gas volume is small. Unfortunately, there are two versions that occur in science and industry.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the first version only
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle V_{mSRK}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               V
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                m
               </mi>
               <mi>
                S
               </mi>
               <mi>
                R
               </mi>
               <mi>
                K
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle V_{mSRK}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="{\displaystyle V_{mSRK}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bbee09529d2513deff97d280d5361b28357cb57a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.799ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
       </span>
       is translated,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soave1990_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Soave1990-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zeberg2001_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Zeberg2001-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the EOS becomes
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle p={\frac {R\,T}{V_{m}+c-b}}-{\frac {a}{\left(V_{m}+c\right)\left(V_{m}+c+b\right)}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  R
                 </mi>
                 <mspace width="thinmathspace">
                 </mspace>
                 <mi>
                  T
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   V
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>

       where the Rackett compressibility factor

       </span>

        </span>
       </dd>

      <p>
       A nice feature with the volume translation method of Peneloux et alios (1982) is that it does not affect the vapor-liquid equilibrium calculations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knudsen1992_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Knudsen1992-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It should be noted that this method of volume translation can also be applied to other cubic EOSs if the c-parameter correlation is adjusted to match the selected EOS.
      </p>

       <span id="Peng.E2.80.93Robinson_equation_of_state">
