        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \omega }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              ω
              <!-- ω -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \omega }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\omega " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/48eff443f9de7a985bb94ca3bde20813ea737be8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.446ex; height:1.676ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Acentric_factor" title="Acentric factor">
        acentric factor
       </a>
       of the species,
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle R}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              R
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle R}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="R" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4b0bfb3769bf24d80e15374dc37b0441e2616e33" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_gas_constant" title="Universal gas constant">
        universal gas constant
       </a>
       and Z=PV/nRT is
       <a href="/wiki/Compressibility_factor" title="Compressibility factor">
        compressibility factor
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Peng–Robinson equation of state (PR EOS) was developed in 1976 at The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">
        University of Alberta
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Ding_Yu_Peng" title="Ding Yu Peng">
        Ding-Yu Peng
       </a>
       and Donald Robinson in order to satisfy the following goals:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        The parameters should be expressible in terms of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critical_properties" title="Critical properties">
         critical properties
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Acentric_factor" title="Acentric factor">
         acentric factor
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The model should provide reasonable accuracy near the critical point, particularly for calculations of the
        <a href="/wiki/Compressibility_factor" title="Compressibility factor">
         compressibility factor
        </a>
        and liquid density.
       </li>
       <li>
        The mixing rules should not employ more than a single binary interaction parameter, which should be independent of temperature pressure and composition.
       </li>
       <li>
        The equation should be applicable to all calculations of all fluid properties in natural gas processes.
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       For the most part the Peng–Robinson equation exhibits performance similar to the Soave equation, although it is generally superior in predicting the liquid densities of many materials, especially nonpolar ones.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Departure_function" title="Departure function">
        departure functions
       </a>
       of the Peng–Robinson equation are given on a separate article.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Peng.E2.80.93Robinson-Stryjek-Vera_equations_of_state">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Peng–Robinson-Stryjek-Vera_equations_of_state">
        <span id="prsv">
        </span>
        Peng–Robinson-Stryjek-Vera equations of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Peng–Robinson-Stryjek-Vera equations of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="PRSV1">
        PRSV1
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: PRSV1">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       A modification to the attraction term in the Peng–Robinson equation of state published by Stryjek and Vera in 1986 (PRSV) significantly improved the model's accuracy by introducing an adjustable pure component parameter and by modifying the polynomial fit of the
       <a href="/wiki/Acentric_factor" title="Acentric factor">
        acentric factor
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRSV1_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PRSV1-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The modification is:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">

       </span>

       <span class="mwe-math-element">

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="PRSV2">
        PRSV2
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: PRSV2">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       A subsequent modification published in 1986 (PRSV2) further improved the model's accuracy by introducing two additional pure component parameters to the previous attraction term modification.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRSV2_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PRSV2-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The modification is:
      </p>

        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \,\kappa _{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mspace width="thinmathspace">
             </mspace>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               κ
               <!-- κ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mn>
                1
               </mn>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \,\kappa _{1}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\,\kappa_1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/432f79e982ed71da542f0feb6ed4ef32680e8efb" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.78ex; height:2.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \,\kappa _{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mspace width="thinmathspace">
             </mspace>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               κ
               <!-- κ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mn>
                2
               </mn>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \,\kappa _{2}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\,\kappa_2" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0bc6043919061d335905b019f64c9349e46bb420" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.78ex; height:2.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       , and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \,\kappa _{3}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mspace width="thinmathspace">
             </mspace>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               κ
               <!-- κ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mn>
                3
               </mn>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \,\kappa _{3}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\,\kappa_3" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a5f065dce96fd58243ee5d1f26a245075c5f4523" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.78ex; height:2.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       are adjustable pure component parameters.
      </p>
      <p>
       PRSV2 is particularly advantageous for
       <a href="/wiki/Vapor%E2%80%93liquid_equilibrium" title="Vapor–liquid equilibrium">
        VLE
       </a>
       calculations. While PRSV1 does offer an advantage over the Peng–Robinson model for describing thermodynamic behavior, it is still not accurate enough, in general, for phase equilibrium calculations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRSV1_14-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-PRSV1-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The highly non-linear behavior of phase-equilibrium calculation methods tends to amplify what would otherwise be acceptably small errors. It is therefore recommended that PRSV2 be used for equilibrium calculations when applying these models to a design. However, once the equilibrium state has been determined, the phase specific thermodynamic values at equilibrium may be determined by one of several simpler models with a reasonable degree of accuracy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRSV2_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-PRSV2-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One thing to note is that in the PRSV equation, the parameter fit is done in a particular temperature range which is usually below the critical temperature. Above the critical temperature, the PRSV alpha function tends to diverge and become arbitrarily large instead of tending towards 0. Because of this, alternate equations for alpha should be employed above the critical point. This is especially important for systems containing hydrogen which is often found at temperatures far above its critical point. Several alternate formulations have been proposed. Some well known ones are by Twu et all or by Mathias and Copeman.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Elliott.2C_Suresh.2C_Donohue_equation_of_state">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Elliott,_Suresh,_Donohue_equation_of_state">
        Elliott, Suresh, Donohue equation of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Elliott, Suresh, Donohue equation of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Elliott, Suresh, and Donohue (ESD) equation of state was proposed in 1990.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESD_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ESD-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The equation seeks to correct a shortcoming in the Peng–Robinson EOS in that there was an inaccuracy in the van der Waals repulsive term. The EOS accounts for the effect of the shape of a non-polar molecule and can be extended to polymers with the addition of an extra term (not shown). The EOS itself was developed through modeling computer simulations and should capture the essential physics of the size, shape, and hydrogen bonding.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

      <p>
       The characteristic size parameter is related to the shape parameter
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

       </span>
       through
      </p>

       <dd>

                </mrow>
                <mrow>

        </span>
        and
        <span class="mwe-math-element">

        </span>

      <p>
       Noting the relationships between Boltzmann's constant and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_gas_constant" title="Universal gas constant">
        Universal gas constant
       </a>
       , and observing that the number of molecules can be expressed in terms of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avogadro%27s_number" title="Avogadro's number">
        Avogadro's number
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Molar_mass" title="Molar mass">
        molar mass
       </a>
       , the reduced number density
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \eta }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

       </span>
       can be expressed in terms of the molar volume as
      </p>

           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="k_1 = 1.7745" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d297819bed984a384fdecda72d467d789b6fad22" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.823ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
        for spherical molecules (c=1)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle k_{2}=1.0617}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>

               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>

                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               1.0617
              </mn>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle k_{2}=1.0617}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="k_2 = 1.0617" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1ca01d3caf3458e7fe5d51e508bf3991377b5880" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.823ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
        for spherical molecules (c=1)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle k_{3}=1.90476.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                k
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 3
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               1.90476.
              </mn>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle k_{3}=1.90476.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="k_3 = 1.90476." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/51b7f6db11e28e78f9a3cc3bcd12fdfecff6a783" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:13.632ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The model can be extended to associating components and mixtures of nonassociating components. Details are in the paper by J.R. Elliott, Jr.
       <i>
        et al.
       </i>
       (1990).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESD_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ESD-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Virial_equations_of_state">
        Virial equations of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Virial equations of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Virial_equation_of_state">
        Virial equation of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Virial equation of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Virial_expansion" title="Virial expansion">
        Virial expansion
       </a>
      </div>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {pV_{m}}{RT}}=A+{\frac {B}{V_{m}}}+{\frac {C}{V_{m}^{2}}}+{\frac {D}{V_{m}^{3}}}+\dots }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   V
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    m
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  R
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  T
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               A
              </mi>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mi>
                 B
                </mi>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  V
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   m
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mi>
                 C
                </mi>
                <msubsup>
                 <mi>
                  V
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   m
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msubsup>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mi>
                 D
                </mi>
                <msubsup>
                 <mi>
                  V
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   m
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   3
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msubsup>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mo>
               …
               <!-- … -->
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\frac {pV_{m}}{RT}}=A+{\frac {B}{V_{m}}}+{\frac {C}{V_{m}^{2}}}+{\frac {D}{V_{m}^{3}}}+\dots }
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {pV_{m}}{RT}}=A+{\frac {B}{V_{m}}}+{\frac {C}{V_{m}^{2}}}+{\frac {D}{V_{m}^{3}}}+\dots }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/33f1a42538606627826558ff3cc5da35eaa6b092" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:35.561ex; height:6.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Although usually not the most convenient equation of state, the virial equation is important because it can be derived directly from
       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">
        statistical mechanics
       </a>
       . This equation is also called the
       <a href="/wiki/Kamerlingh_Onnes" title="Kamerlingh Onnes">
        Kamerlingh Onnes
       </a>
       equation. If appropriate assumptions are made about the mathematical form of intermolecular forces, theoretical expressions can be developed for each of the
       <a href="/wiki/Virial_coefficient" title="Virial coefficient">
        coefficients
       </a>
       .
       <i>
        A
       </i>
       is the first virial coefficient, which has a constant value of 1 and makes the statement that when volume is large, all fluids behave like ideal gases. The second virial coefficient
       <i>
        B
       </i>
       corresponds to interactions between pairs of molecules,
       <i>
        C
       </i>
       to triplets, and so on. Accuracy can be increased indefinitely by considering higher order terms. The coefficients
       <i>
        B
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        C
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        D
       </i>
       , etc. are functions of temperature only.
      </p>
      <p>
       One of the most accurate equations of state is that from Benedict-Webb-Rubin-Starling
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       shown next. It was very close to a virial equation of state. If the exponential term in it is expanded to two Taylor terms, a virial equation can be derived:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle p=\rho RT+\left(B_{0}RT-A_{0}-{\frac {C_{0}}{T^{2}}}+{\frac {D_{0}}{T^{3}}}-{\frac {E_{0}}{T^{4}}}\right)\rho ^{2}+\left(bRT-a-{\frac {d}{T}}+{\frac {c}{T^{2}}}\right)\rho ^{3}+\alpha \left(a+{\frac {d}{T}}\right)\rho ^{6}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mi>
               R
              </mi>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  B
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   0
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mi>
                 R
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 T
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <msub>
                 <mi>
                  A
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   0
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <msub>
                   <mi>
                    C
                   </mi>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     0
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <msup>
                   <mi>
                    T
                   </mi>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     2
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msup>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <msub>
                   <mi>
                    D
                   </mi>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     0
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <msup>
                   <mi>
                    T
                   </mi>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     3
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msup>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <msub>
                   <mi>
                    E
                   </mi>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     0
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <msup>
                   <mi>
                    T
                   </mi>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     4
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msup>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                ρ
                <!-- ρ -->
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow>
                <mi>
                 b
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 R
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 T
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mi>
                 a
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <mi>
                   d
                  </mi>
                  <mi>
                   T
                  </mi>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <mi>
                   c
                  </mi>
                  <msup>
                   <mi>
                    T
                   </mi>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     2
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msup>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                ρ
                <!-- ρ -->
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 3
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mi>
               α
               <!-- α -->
              </mi>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow>
                <mi>
                 a
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <mi>
                   d
                  </mi>
                  <mi>
                   T
                  </mi>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                ρ
                <!-- ρ -->
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 6
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle p=\rho RT+\left(B_{0}RT-A_{0}-{\frac {C_{0}}{T^{2}}}+{\frac {D_{0}}{T^{3}}}-{\frac {E_{0}}{T^{4}}}\right)\rho ^{2}+\left(bRT-a-{\frac {d}{T}}+{\frac {c}{T^{2}}}\right)\rho ^{3}+\alpha \left(a+{\frac {d}{T}}\right)\rho ^{6}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle p=\rho RT+\left(B_{0}RT-A_{0}-{\frac {C_{0}}{T^{2}}}+{\frac {D_{0}}{T^{3}}}-{\frac {E_{0}}{T^{4}}}\right)\rho ^{2}+\left(bRT-a-{\frac {d}{T}}+{\frac {c}{T^{2}}}\right)\rho ^{3}+\alpha \left(a+{\frac {d}{T}}\right)\rho ^{6}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/42ee89a022e53bac20f356c4cbcdcda69f955d75" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:95.736ex; height:6.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Note that in this virial equation, the fourth and fifth virial terms are zero. The second virial coefficient is monotonically decreasing as temperature is lowered. The third virial coefficient is monotonically increasing as temperature is lowered.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_BWR_equation_of_state">
        The BWR equation of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

         ]
        </span>

       </dd>

        K.E. Starling (1973).
        <i>
         Fluid Properties for Light Petroleum Systems
        </i>
        .
        <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Publishing_Company" title="Gulf Publishing Company">
         Gulf Publishing Company
        </a>
        .
       </cite>
       <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Fluid+Properties+for+Light+Petroleum+Systems&amp;rft.pub=Gulf+Publishing+Company&amp;rft.date=1973&amp;rft.au=K.E.+Starling&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEquation+of+state">
        <span style="display:none;">
        </span>

      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="SAFT_equations_of_state">
        SAFT equations of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: SAFT equations of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Statistical_associating_fluid_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Statistical associating fluid theory (page does not exist)">
        Statistical associating fluid theory
       </a>
       (SAFT) equations of state use
       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">
        statistical mechanical
       </a>
       methods (in particular
       <a href="/wiki/Perturbation_theory" title="Perturbation theory">
        perturbation theory
       </a>
       ) to describe the interactions between molecules in a system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The idea of a SAFT equation of state was first proposed by Chapman et al. in 1989,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_18-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but since then many different SAFT equations of state have been proposed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Often SAFT equations represent molecules as collections of spherical particles that interact with one another.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_18-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One popular SAFT equation represents molecules as chains composed of spherical segments (PC-SAFT).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In general, SAFT equations give more accurate results than traditional cubic equations of state, especially for systems containing liquids or solids.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Multiparameter_equations_of_state">
        Multiparameter equations of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Multiparameter equations of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Helmholtz_Function_form">
        Helmholtz Function form
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Helmholtz Function form">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Multiparameter equations of state (MEOS) can be used to represent pure fluids with high accuracy, in both the liquid and gaseous states. MEOS's represent the Helmholtz function of the fluid as the sum of ideal gas and residual terms. Both terms are explicit in reduced temperature and reduced density - thus:
      </p>
      <p>
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {a(T,\rho )}{RT}}={\frac {a^{o}(T,\rho )+a^{r}(T,\rho )}{RT}}=\alpha ^{o}(\tau ,\delta )+\alpha ^{r}(\tau ,\delta )}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mfrac>
               <mrow>
                <mi>
                 a
                </mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 (
                </mo>
                <mi>
                 T

                <mo>
                 ,
                </mo>
                <mi>
                 ρ
                 <!-- ρ -->
                </mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 )
                </mo>
               </mrow>
               <mrow>
                <mi>
                 R
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 T
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </mfrac>
             </mrow>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mfrac>
               <mrow>
                <msup>
                 <mi>
                  a
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   o
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </msup>
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 (

                 ,
                </mo>

                </mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 )
                </mo>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <msup>
                 <mi>
                  a
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   r
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </msup>
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 (
                </mo>
                <mi>
                 T
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 ,
                </mo>
                <mi>
                 ρ
                 <!-- ρ -->
                </mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 )
                </mo>
               </mrow>
               <mrow>
                <mi>
                 R
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 T
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </mfrac>
             </mrow>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <msup>
              <mi>
               α
               <!-- α -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                o
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msup>
             <mo stretchy="false">
              (
             </mo>
             <mi>
              τ
              <!-- τ -->
             </mi>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <mi>

              <!-- δ -->
             </mi>

             </mo>

              <mi>
               α
               <!-- α -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                r
               </mi>

             </mo>

              <!-- τ -->
             </mi>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <mi>
              δ
              <!-- δ -->
             </mi>
             <mo stretchy="false">
              )
             </mo>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle {\frac {a(T,\rho )}{RT}}={\frac {a^{o}(T,\rho )+a^{r}(T,\rho )}{RT}}=\alpha ^{o}(\tau ,\delta )+\alpha ^{r}(\tau ,\delta )}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt=" \frac{a(T,\rho)}{RT} = 
\frac{a^o(T,\rho)+a^r(T,\rho)}{RT}=
\alpha^o(\tau,\delta)+
\alpha^r(\tau,\delta)
" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0901058cb51a577e67b86b09cc67bd452fd30cf8" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:51.453ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
       </span>
      </p>
      <p>
       Where:
      </p>
      <p>
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \tau ={\frac {T_{r}}{T}},\delta ={\frac {\rho }{\rho _{r}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              τ
              <!-- τ -->
             </mi>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mfrac>
               <msub>
                <mi>
                 T
                </mi>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi>
                  r
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </msub>
               <mi>
                T
               </mi>
              </mfrac>
             </mrow>
             <mo>
              ,
             </mo>
             <mi>
              δ
              <!-- δ -->
             </mi>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mfrac>
               <mi>
                ρ
                <!-- ρ -->
               </mi>
               <msub>
                <mi>
                 ρ
                 <!-- ρ -->
                </mi>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi>
                  r
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </msub>
              </mfrac>
             </mrow>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \tau ={\frac {T_{r}}{T}},\delta ={\frac {\rho }{\rho _{r}}}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt=" \tau = \frac{T_r}{T},    \delta = \frac{\rho}{\rho_r} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e18523f341f5d3333f7d69565b54b31954377e99" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:15.661ex; height:5.676ex;"/>
       </span>
      </p>
      <p>
       The reduced density and temperature are typically, though not always, the critical values for the pure fluid. Other thermodynamic functions can be derived from the MEOS by using appropriate derivatives of the Helmholtz function; hence, because integration of the MEOS is not required, there are few restrictions as to the functional form of the ideal or residual terms. Typical MEOS use upwards of 50 fluid specific parameters, but are able to represent the fluid's properties with high accuracy. MEOS are available currently for about 50 of the most common industrial fluids including refrigerants. Mixture models also exist.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_equations_of_state_of_interest">
        Other equations of state of interest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Other equations of state of interest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Stiffened_equation_of_state">
        Stiffened equation of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Stiffened equation of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       When considering water under very high pressures, in situations such as
       <a href="/wiki/Underwater_explosion" title="Underwater explosion">
        underwater nuclear explosions
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extracorporeal_shock_wave_lithotripsy" title="Extracorporeal shock wave lithotripsy">
        sonic shock lithotripsy
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Sonoluminescence" title="Sonoluminescence">
        sonoluminescence
       </a>
       , the stiffened equation of state is often used:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle p=\rho (\gamma -1)e-\gamma p^{0}\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mi>
               γ
               <!-- γ -->
              </mi>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mn>
               1
              </mn>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mi>
               e
              </mi>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mi>
               γ
               <!-- γ -->
              </mi>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 0
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle p=\rho (\gamma -1)e-\gamma p^{0}\,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt=" p=\rho(\gamma-1)e-\gamma p^0 \," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b1a3f6be05e9aca8e44038351b640dcc18240e10" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:20.431ex; height:3.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle e}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              e
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle e}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="e" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cd253103f0876afc68ebead27a5aa9867d927467" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.083ex; height:1.676ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the internal energy per unit mass,
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \gamma }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              γ
              <!-- γ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \gamma }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\gamma " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a223c880b0ce3da8f64ee33c4f0010beee400b1a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:1.262ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       is an empirically determined constant typically taken to be about 6.1, and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle p^{0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msup>
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mn>
                0
               </mn>
              </mrow>
             </msup>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle p^{0}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="p^0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/92a2e2fda83d61a09cadf00ac7a1e4545d7584b0" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:2.313ex; height:3.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       is another constant, representing the molecular attraction between water molecules. The magnitude of the correction is about 2 gigapascals (20,000 atmospheres).
      </p>
      <p>
       The equation is stated in this form because the speed of sound in water is given by
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle c^{2}=\gamma (p+p^{0})/\rho }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msup>
              <mi>
               c
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mn>
                2
               </mn>
              </mrow>
             </msup>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <mi>
              γ
              <!-- γ -->
             </mi>
             <mo stretchy="false">
              (
             </mo>
             <mi>
              p
             </mi>
             <mo>
              +
             </mo>
             <msup>
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mn>
                0
               </mn>
              </mrow>
             </msup>
             <mo stretchy="false">
              )
             </mo>
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mo>
               /
              </mo>
             </mrow>
             <mi>
              ρ
              <!-- ρ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle c^{2}=\gamma (p+p^{0})/\rho }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="c^2=\gamma(p+p^0)/\rho" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54f41df469709f1e200f40bb673d7ef4fcb25041" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:16.829ex; height:3.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Thus water behaves as though it is an ideal gas that is
       <i>
        already
       </i>
       under about 20,000 atmospheres (2 GPa) pressure, and explains why water is commonly assumed to be incompressible: when the external pressure changes from 1 atmosphere to 2 atmospheres (100 kPa to 200 kPa), the water behaves as an ideal gas would when changing from 20,001 to 20,002 atmospheres (2000.1 MPa to 2000.2 MPa).
      </p>
      <p>
       This equation mispredicts the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_heat_capacity" title="Specific heat capacity">
        specific heat capacity
       </a>
       of water but few simple alternatives are available for severely nonisentropic processes such as strong shocks.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ultrarelativistic_equation_of_state">
        Ultrarelativistic equation of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ultrarelativistic equation of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       An
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultrarelativistic_fluid" title="Ultrarelativistic fluid">
        ultrarelativistic fluid
       </a>
       has equation of state
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle p=\rho _{m}c_{s}^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                ρ
                <!-- ρ -->
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <msubsup>
               <mi>
                c
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 s
                </mi>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msubsup>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle p=\rho _{m}c_{s}^{2}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="p=\rho_m c_s^2" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/65c7d8cba974e260ed0cff2b621d3738cd24f4c4" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:9.295ex; height:3.009ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              p
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle p}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the pressure,
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \rho _{m}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                m
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \rho _{m}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\rho_m" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fb8e01f5f9a1ec7641573c415df8bfa942a42a78" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:2.877ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the mass density, and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{s}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <msub>
              <mi>
               c
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                s
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle c_{s}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="c_{s}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/75b83e050da28fa0d83e2aa786963805742ab756" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.01ex; height:2.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_sound" title="Speed of sound">
        speed of sound
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ideal_Bose_equation_of_state">
        Ideal Bose equation of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equation_of_state&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Ideal Bose equation of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The equation of state for an ideal
       <a href="/wiki/Bose_gas" title="Bose gas">
        Bose gas
       </a>
       is
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle pV_{m}=RT~{\frac {{\textrm {Li}}_{\alpha +1}(z)}{\zeta (\alpha )}}\left({\frac {T}{T_{c}}}\right)^{\alpha }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                V
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               R
              </mi>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mtext>
              </mtext>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <msub>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mtext>
                     Li
                    </mtext>
                   </mrow>
                  </mrow>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    α
                    <!-- α -->
                   </mi>
                   <mo>
                    +
                   </mo>
                   <mn>
                    1
                   </mn>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                 <mo stretchy="false">
                  (
                 </mo>
                 <mi>
                  z
                 </mi>
                 <mo stretchy="false">
                  )
                 </mo>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  ζ
                  <!-- ζ -->
                 </mi>
                 <mo stretchy="false">
                  (
                 </mo>
                 <mi>
                  α
                  <!-- α -->
                 </mi>
                 <mo stretchy="false">
                  )
                 </mo>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <msup>
               <mrow>
                <mo>
                 (
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <mi>
                   T
                  </mi>
                  <msub>
                   <mi>
                    T
                   </mi>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mi>
                     c
                    </mi>
                   </mrow>
                  </msub>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 )
                </mo>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 α
                 <!-- α -->
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle pV_{m}=RT~{\frac {{\textrm {Li}}_{\alpha +1}(z)}{\zeta (\alpha )}}\left({\frac {T}{T_{c}}}\right)^{\alpha }}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="pV_m=RT~\frac{\textrm{Li}_{\alpha+1}(z)}{\zeta(\alpha)}
\left(\frac{T}{T_c}\right)^\alpha" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7499f5a01cd3b107fa91243dbca09568e7b3dbe9" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:28.43ex; height:6.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where α is an exponent specific to the system (e.g. in the absence of a potential field, α=3/2),
       <i>
        z
       </i>
       is exp(
       <i>
        μ
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        kT
       </i>
       ) where
       <i>
        μ
       </i>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_potential" title="Chemical potential">
        chemical potential
       </a>
       , Li is the
       <a href="/wiki/Polylogarithm" title="Polylogarithm">
        polylogarithm
       </a>
       , ζ is the
       <a href="/wiki/Riemann_zeta_function" title="Riemann zeta function">
        Riemann zeta function
       </a>
       , and
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       <sub>
        <i>
         c
        </i>
       </sub>
       is the critical temperature at which a
       <a href="/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_condensate" title="Bose–Einstein condensate">
        Bose–Einstein condensate
       </a>
       begins to form.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Jones.E2.80.93Wilkins.E2.80.93Lee_equation_of_state_for_explosives_.28JWL_equation.29">

            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle p=A\cdot \left(1-{\frac {\omega }{R_{1}\cdot V}}\right)\cdot \exp(-R_{1}\cdot V)+B\cdot \left(1-{\frac {\omega }{R_{2}\cdot V}}\right)\cdot \exp(-R_{2}\cdot V)+{\frac {\omega \cdot e_{0}}{V}}}

          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt=" p=A \cdot \left( 1 - \frac{\omega}{R_1 \cdot V} \right)  \cdot \exp (-R_1 \cdot V) + B \cdot \left( 1 - \frac{\omega}{R_2 \cdot V} \right) \cdot \exp (-R_2 \cdot V) + \frac{\omega \cdot e_0}{V} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/13f66fc431c2a35d5f88f9e67e3d3108d013cf2c" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:82.359ex; height:6.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The ratio
       <span class="mwe-math-element">

       is defined by using
       <span class="mwe-math-element">

       </span>
       = density of the detonation products. The parameters

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Equations_of_state_for_solids_and_liquids">

                   <mi mathvariant="normal">
                    Δ
                    <!-- Δ -->
                   </mi>
                   <mi>
                    p
                   </mi>
                  </mtd>

                </mo>

              </mtext>

              </mo>

              <mi>

              </mi>
              <mo>

              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>

                  <mrow>
                  </mrow>

                 <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">

                  <mrow>
                  </mrow>
                 </mpadded>
                 <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    V
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </mstyle>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mn>
               1
              </mn>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle p(V)={\begin{cases}k_{1}~\xi +k_{2}~\xi ^{2}+k_{3}~\xi ^{3}+\Delta p&amp;\qquad {\text{Compression}}\\k_{1}~\xi &amp;\qquad {\text{Tension}}\end{cases}}~;~~\xi :={\cfrac {V_{0}}{V}}-1}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>

        </span>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        where
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

        </span>
        is the bulk modulus at equilibrium volume
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle V_{0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

             {\displaystyle V_{0}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt=" V_0 " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7ae15ff9b845587dc4e1816f59c3fed0e71a132f" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.409ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
        and
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

        </span>
        typically about -2 is often related to the
        <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCneisen_parameter" title="Grüneisen parameter">
